        8 days, 17 hours, 54 minutes\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="display:none">\n        <td colspan="2">\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" href="/wiki/Richard_Mastracchio" title="Richard Mastracchio">\n          Mastracchio\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Morgan" title="Barbara Morgan">\n          Morgan\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Charles_O._Hobaugh" title="Charles O. Hobaugh">\n          Hobaugh\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Scott_Kelly_(astronaut)" title="Scott Kelly (astronaut)">\n          Kelly\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Caldwell_Dyson" title="Tracy Caldwell Dyson">\n          Caldwell\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Williams" title="Dafydd Williams">\n          Williams\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Drew" title="Alvin Drew">\n          Drew\n         </a>\n         .\n         <div class="" style="width:100%; text-align:center; border-top:1px #aaa solid">\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n           Space Shuttle program\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div style="width:100%">\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: left; text-align:left;padding-right:0.5em;">\n           \xe2\x86\x90\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-117" title="STS-117">\n            STS-117\n           </a>\n          </div>\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: right; text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;">\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-120" title="STS-120">\n            STS-120\n           </a>\n           \xe2\x86\x92\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        STS-118\n       </b>\n       was a\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        space shuttle\n       </a>\n       mission to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS) flown by the orbiter\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n         Endeavour\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . STS-118 lifted off on 8 August 2007 from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n        launch pad 39A\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       (KSC), Florida and landed at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Landing_Facility" title="Shuttle Landing Facility">\n        Shuttle Landing Facility\n       </a>\n       at KSC on 21 August 2007.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This was the first flight of\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       since\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-113" title="STS-113">\n        STS-113\n       </a>\n       in November 2002, which was also the last successful shuttle flight before\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n        STS-107\n       </a>\n       which culminated in the loss of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n         Columbia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       when it\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        disintegrated during reentry\n       </a>\n       . STS-118 pilot Charles Hobaugh had been the entry team\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CAPCOM" title="CAPCOM">\n        CAPCOM\n       </a>\n       for STS-107.\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       would have been chosen for this mission,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       for what would have been its 29th mission, and its first and likely its only mission to the ISS.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The mission is also referred to as\n       <b>\n        ISS-13A.1\n       </b>\n       by the ISS program. The mission added two more components to the ISS and brought supplies for its crew.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During and after the mission, the media focused heavily on a small puncture in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermal_Protection_System" title="Thermal Protection System">\n        heat shield\n       </a>\n       , created by a piece of insulation foam that came off the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n        external tank\n       </a>\n       during liftoff, though the foam impact that ultimately destroyed\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       caused more damage and was in a critical area. KSC Launch Director\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Leinbach" title="Michael D. Leinbach">\n        Michael D. Leinbach\n       </a>\n       mentioned in the post-flight news conference that upon initial inspection on the ground, "\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       appears to be the \'cleanest\' post-flight orbiter since\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-114" title="STS-114">\n        Return to Flight\n       </a>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 31 August 2007, NASA reported that the damaged tiles had been removed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Processing_Facility" title="Orbiter Processing Facility">\n        Orbiter Processing Facility\n       </a>\n       , and engineers had found no evidence of heat-related damage to the orbiter itself.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a   <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n       <tr>\n        <th style="width:150px;">\n         <a href="/wiki/Astronaut_ranks_and_positions" title="Astronaut ranks and positions">\n          Position\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <th colspan="2" scope="col" style="width:200px;">\n         Astronaut\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Commander\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Scott_Kelly_(astronaut)" Caldwell\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         First spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 2\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Richard_Mastracchio" title="Richard Mastracchio">\n          Richard A. Alvin Drew\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         First spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crew_notes">\n        Crew notes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Crew notes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Astronaut\n       <a href="/wiki/Clayton_Anderson" title="Clayton Anderson">\n        Clayton Anderson\n       </a>\n       originally was slated to be launched to the ISS on this mission, but was moved to\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-117" title="STS-117">\n        STS-117\n       </a>\n       . His replacement was\n       <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Drew" title="Alvin Drew">\n        Alvin Drew\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA press releases and media briefing documents stated that STS-118 was the first flight of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Educator_Astronaut_Project" title="Educator Astronaut Project">\n        Mission Specialist Educator\n       </a>\n       due to the presence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Morgan" title="Barbara Morgan">\n        Barbara Morgan\n       </a>\n       . The Educator Astronaut Project is the successor to\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Teacher_in_Space_Project" title="Teacher in Space Project">\n        Teacher in Space Project\n       </a>\n       , which ended with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        Space Shuttle Challenger disaster\n       </a>\n       in 1986.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Also, the official STS-118 mission patch included a flame of knowledge that represented the importance of education, and honored teachers and students everywhere. The tip of the flames touched Morgan\'s name on the patch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-patch_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-patch-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_Administrator" title="NASA Administrator">\n        NASA Administrator\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Griffin" title="Michael D. Griffin">\n        Michael D. Griffin\n       </a>\n       clarified at a post-mission press conference that Morgan was not considered a Mission Specialist Educator, but rather a standard Mission Specialist, who had once been a teacher.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michael118_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-michael118-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Prior to the\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       disaster, the crew manifest for STS-118 was:\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">\n       <tr>\n        <th style="width:150px;">\n         <a href="/wiki/Astronaut_ranks_and_positions" title="Astronaut ranks and positions">\n          Position\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <th colspan="2" scope="col" style="width:200px;">\n         Astronaut\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Commander\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Scott_Kelly_(astronaut)" title="Scott Kelly (astronaut)">\n          Scott J. Hobaugh">\n          Charles O. Parazynski">\n          Scott E. Parazynski\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Fifth spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 2\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Williams" title="Dafydd Williams">\n          Dafydd R. Williams\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">\n          CSA\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Second spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 3\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Nowak" title="Lisa Nowak">\n          Lisa M. Nowak\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         First spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 4\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Morgan" title="Barbara Morgan">\n          Barbara R. Morgan\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         First spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="3">\n         Parazynski was assigned to\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-120" title="STS-120">\n          STS-120\n         </a>\n         and Nowak was assigned to\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-121" title="STS-121">\n          STS-121\n         </a>\n         .\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_payloads">\n        Mission payloads\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mission payloads">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ESP-3_aspect_Full.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="447" data-file-width="1230" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/ESP-3_aspect_Full.png/220px-ESP-3_aspect_Full.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/ESP-3_aspect_Full.png/330px-ESP-3_aspect_Full.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/ESP-3_aspect_Full.png/440px-ESP-3_aspect_Full.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ESP-3_aspect_Full.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         ESP-3 launch configuration\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sts-118_cargo.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3008" data-file-width="2000" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sts-118_cargo.jpg/220px-Sts-118_cargo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sts-118_cargo.jpg/330px-Sts-118_cargo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sts-118_cargo.jpg/440px-Sts-118_cargo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sts-118_cargo.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         From top to bottom: Orbiter docking system, Spacehab, S5 truss, ESP-3. The CMG is the globe bottom left.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The STS-118 mission delivered and assembled the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Starboard" title="Starboard">\n        starboard\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P5_spacer_truss_segment" title="P5 spacer truss segment">\n        S5 truss\n       </a>\n       segment of the International Space Station, as well as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/External_Stowage_Platform" title="External Stowage Platform">\n        External Stowage Platform 3\n       </a>\n       , (ESP-3) and a replacement\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Control_Moment_Gyroscope" title="Control Moment Gyroscope">\n        Control Moment Gyroscope\n       </a>\n       (CMG). The mission was also the final flight to include the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacehab" title="Spacehab">\n        Spacehab\n       </a>\n       Logistics Single Module.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Spacehab Logistics Single Module, a pressurized aluminum habitat that is carried inside the payload bay, has a capacity of 6,000 pounds (2,700\xc2\xa0kg), and carried a variety of cargo and research projects, including supply materials for the ISS. It returned cargo, including the MISSE PEC 3 &amp; 4, a\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">\n        Department of Defense\n       </a>\n       payload that had been installed on the ISS. Launched in July 2006, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Materials_International_Space_Station_Experiment" title="Materials International Space Station Experiment">\n        MISSE PEC-3 &amp; 4\n       </a>\n       contained over 850 materials specimens that will be studied to determine the effects of long-term exposure to the environment of space.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n 1\xe2\x80\x932\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Orbiter Docking System\n         <br/>\n         <a href="/wiki/Extravehicular_Mobility_Unit" title="Extravehicular Mobility Unit">\n          EMU\n         </a>\n         3010 / EMU 3017\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1,800 kilograms (4,000\xc2\xa0lb)?\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Bay 3\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Tunnel Adapter\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         112 kilograms (247\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Bay 5\xe2\x80\x937\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Spacehab-SM\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         5,480 kilograms (12,080\xc2\xa0lb)?\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Bay 8P\n Platform">\n          ESP-3\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         3,400 kilograms (7,500\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Sill\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Boom_Sensor_System" title="Orbiter Boom Sensor System">\n          OBSS\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         450 kilograms (990\xc2\xa0lb)?\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Sill\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Canadarm" title="Canadarm">\n          RMS\n         </a>\n         201\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         390 kilograms (860\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Total:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          14,036 kilograms (30,944\xc2\xa0lb)\n         </b>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_background">\n        Mission background\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mission background">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS118.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/ISS_after_STS118.jpg/220px-ISS_after_STS118.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/ISS_after_STS118.jpg/330px-ISS_after_STS118.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/ISS_after_STS118.jpg/440px-ISS_after_STS118.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS118.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         New components added to the International Space Station after flight STS-118/13A.1. (NASA)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The mission was originally scheduled to be flown by\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       ; STS-118 would have marked that orbiter\'s 29th flight and its first visit to the International Space Station. However, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        disaster\n       </a>\n       altered the planned flight schedules, and the mission was rescheduled for\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       . STS-118 served as\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\'\n       </i>\n       s return to flight after a planned orbiter re-fit and maintenance period that resulted in over 200 modifications to the orbiter.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fox-refit_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fox-refit-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       One of the most important modifications that debuted during STS-118 is an upgraded power-distribution module, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrical_system_of_the_International_Space_Station" title="Electrical system of the International Space Station">\n        Station-Shuttle Power Transfer System\n       </a>\n       (SSPTS). SSPTS allows\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       to tap into the ISS power supply, converting up to eight kilowatts of electrical power from 120-volts direct-current (120VDC) ISS main voltage to the 28VDC system used by the orbiter. SSPTS was outfitted to the ISS\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressurized_Mating_Adapter" title="Pressurized Mating Adapter">\n        Pressurized Mating Adapter\n       </a>\n       -2 (PMA2) during\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-116" title="STS-116">\n        STS-116\n       </a>\n       . These upgrades will allow orbiters to remain docked at the station for an additional three to four mission days\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       by saving cryogenic liquid hydrogen and oxygen needed to run the fuel cells which generate electricity aboard the orbiter; oxygen and hydrogen tank capacity is a major factor limiting the duration of orbiter free flights. Other systems debuting on this flight were a three-string\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">\n        GPS\n       </a>\n       system, which replaces the three\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tactical_Air_Navigation" title="Tactical Air Navigation">\n        Tactical Air Navigation\n       </a>\n       -units, used to guide the shuttle and calculate its position during reentry and landing and the new Advanced Health Management System which keeps an eye on the three main engines (SSMEs) during liftoff and will shut them down before any catastrophic damage might develop. (All SSMEs had their own computers to regulate, monitor, and shut them down in case of trouble; the new system extends and improves the monitoring capability for increased safety.)\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       also received several systems that the other orbiters had already been equipped with, such as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Glass_cockpit" title="Glass cockpit">\n        glass cockpit\n       </a>\n       , improved wing leading-edge sensors and the OBSS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fox-refit_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fox-refit-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       STS-118 included mission specialist\n       <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Morgan" title="Barbara Morgan">\n        Barbara Morgan\n       </a>\n       , the first Mission Specialist Educator. Morgan trained as the backup to\n       <a href="/wiki/Christa_McAuliffe" title="Christa McAuliffe">\n        Christa McAuliffe\n       </a>\n       , NASA\'s Teacher in Space candidate from 1985 to 1986. McAuliffe was killed in the space shuttle\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Challenger_accident" title="Challenger accident">\n        <i>\n         Challenger\n        </i>\n        accident\n       </a>\n       on 28 January 1986. While McAuliffe and Morgan were classified as spaceflight participants and not as mission specialists in 1986, after the Teacher in Space Project was canceled, Morgan assumed the duties of Teacher in Space Designee and continued to work with NASA\'s Education Division until her selection as NASA\'s first Mission Specialist Educator in 1998. Morgan completed two years of training and evaluation and began official duties in 2000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An Educator Astronaut is a fully trained astronaut who performs all the same duties that a regular astronaut does.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Morgan became the first Mission Specialist Educator in space on STS-118, and will share what she learned from the experience with students during and after her flight.\n      </p>\n      <table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n       <tr>\n        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: \'Times New Roman\', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\n         \xe2\x80\x9c\n        </td>\n        <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">\n         <i>\n          Whether you\'re teaching school, or whether you\'re training as an astronaut, you put all you can into it, and get the most out of it.\n         </i>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 Barbara Morgan\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n          <a href="#cite_note-17">\n           [17]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: \'Times New Roman\', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\n         \xe2\x80\x9d\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The mission marked:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        150th manned US space launch\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        119th Space Shuttle flight\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        22nd International Space Station assembly mission\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        20th flight of\n        <i>\n         Endeavour\n        </i>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        94th Post-\n        <i>\n         Challenger\n        </i>\n        mission\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        6th Post-\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        mission\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        First flight with\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSPTS" title="SSPTS">\n         SSPTS\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_timeline">\n        Mission timeline\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mission timeline">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_preparations">\n        Launch preparations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Launch preparations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_Launchpad.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/STS-118_Launchpad.jpg/220px-STS-118_Launchpad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/STS-118_Launchpad.jpg/330px-STS-118_Launchpad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/STS-118_Launchpad.jpg/440px-STS-118_Launchpad.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_Launchpad.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space Shuttle\n         <i>\n          Endeavour\n         </i>\n         arrives at launch pad 39A.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       (OV-105) was moved from the Orbiter Processing Facility, bay OPF-2 to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        Vehicle Assembly Building\n       </a>\n       on 2 July 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 10 July 2007,\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       moved from the Vehicle Assembly Building to Launch Pad 39A. Moving at less than one mile per hour (1.6 kilometres (0.99\xc2\xa0mi)/h) atop the\n       <a href="/wiki/Crawler-transporter" title="Crawler-transporter">\n        crawler-transporter\n       </a>\n       , the move began at 20:10 EDT, and was "hard down" (secured in place at the pad) at 03:02 EDT, 11 July 2007.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The crew completed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Terminal_countdown_demonstration_test" title="Terminal countdown demonstration test">\n        terminal countdown demonstration test\n       </a>\n       on 19 July 2007, and the Flight Readiness Review meetings were held on 25\xe2\x80\x9326 July 2007, after which NASA managers declared STS-118 a "GO" for launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The launch was delayed one day to repair a valve in the shuttle\'s crew cabin pressurization system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harwood_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Harwood-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Commander Kelly and the crew arrived at Kennedy Space Center on 3 August 2007, for final launch preparations. The countdown clock began at 20:00 EDT 5 August 2007, for the launch at 18:36 EDT on 8 August 2007.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Wednesday_8_August_(Flight_day_1,_Launch)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wednesday_8_August_.28Flight_day_1.2C_Launch.29">\n        Wednesday 8 August (Flight day 1, Launch)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Wednesday 8 August (Flight day 1, Launch)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_Endeavour_Launch_2007Aug08_(KSC-07PP-2288).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2122" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/STS-118_Endeavour_Launch_2007Aug08_%28KSC-07PP-2288%29.jpg/220px-STS-118_Endeavour_Launch_2007Aug08_%28KSC-07PP-2288%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/STS-118_Endeavour_Launch_2007Aug08_%28KSC-07PP-2288%29.jpg/330px-STS-118_Endeavour_Launch_2007Aug08_%28KSC-07PP-2288%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/STS-118_Endeavour_Launch_2007Aug08_%28KSC-07PP-2288%29.jpg/440px-STS-118_Endeavour_Launch_2007Aug08_%28KSC-07PP-2288%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_Endeavour_Launch_2007Aug08_(KSC-07PP-2288).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Launch of STS-118.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Fueling of the external tank began at 08:11 EDT (12:11 UTC) and finished around 11:00 EDT. The Ice Team began their inspection of the orbiter to ensure no ice was on the orbiter or the fuel tank, something unlikely due to the unusually warm conditions as launch time approached. Their inspection lasted about 40 minutes shorter than the usual two hours. The crew departed for the Operations &amp; Checkout (O&amp;C) building, for the launch pad at 14:46 EDT (18:46 UTC), and arrived at the pad at 15:02 EDT (19:02 UTC). Launch occurred at 18:36:42 EDT (22:36:42 UTC).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Countdown and launch notes:\n       </b>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The Ice Team members discovered a small crack in the foam surrounding the external fuel tank during their preflight examination. After a review by the Mission Management Team, it was concluded that there was no debris issue regarding the crack, and the tank was safe to fly.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A problem with the switches associated with the crew hatch required a second and third hatch closure attempt. Hatch closure was completed and verified at 17:23 EDT (21:23 UTC).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The high-definition video camera used to inspect the shuttle from Kennedy Space Center during launch failed prior to liftoff. The launch team decided that the cameras on the external tank and the orbiter would be sufficient for observations, and went on to launch without it.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The final forecast predicted 80% go for launch weather.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n         <a href="#cite_note-21">\n          [21]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Launch Director Mike Leinbach conducted his T-9 poll, and declared\n        <i>\n         Endeavour\n        </i>\n        a "go" for launch at 18:26 EDT (22:26 UTC).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Liftoff occurred at 18:36:42\xc2\xa0pm EDT. (22:36:42 UTC)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solid_Rocket_Booster" title="Solid Rocket Booster">\n         Solid Rocket Boosters\n        </a>\n        successfully separated at 18:39\xc2\xa0pm EDT (22:39 UTC).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Main Engine Cutoff occurred at 18:45:30\xc2\xa0pm EDT (22:45:30 UTC)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/External_Tank" title="External Tank">\n         External Tank\n        </a>\n        separation occurred at 18:45:45\xc2\xa0pm EDT (22:45:45 UTC)\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       The primary\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_abort_modes" title="Space Shuttle abort modes">\n        TAL\n       </a>\n       site was\n       <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza_Airport" title="Zaragoza Airport">\n        Zaragoza Airport\n       </a>\n       in Spain.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the procedures for post-ascent, the crew opened the payload bay doors, activated the Spacehab, powered up the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remote_Manipulator_System" title="Remote Manipulator System">\n        Remote Manipulator System\n       </a>\n       , and performed a variety of other payload activation procedures, before entering their scheduled sleep shift at 04:36 UTC (12:36\xc2\xa0am EDT) 9 August 2007.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Thursday_9_August_(Flight_day_2)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Thursday_9_August_.28Flight_day_2.29">\n        Thursday 9 August (Flight day 2)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Thursday 9 August (Flight day 2)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The shuttle crew spent most of the day inspecting the outer hull and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_shuttle_thermal_protection_system" title="Space shuttle thermal protection system">\n        heat shield\n       </a>\n       . During the mission status briefing, Deputy Shuttle Program Manager (and Mission Management Team chairman) John Shannon reported that during launch, approximately nine pieces of foam were observed breaking off the external fuel tanks. Three of these struck the shuttle. All three strikes are considered to be minor in nature.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Friday_10_August_(Flight_day_3)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Friday_10_August_.28Flight_day_3.29">\n        Friday 10 August (Flight day 3)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Friday 10 August (Flight day 3)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_thermal_tile_damage.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="181" data-file-width="220" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4a/STS-118_thermal_tile_damage.jpg" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_thermal_tile_damage.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Preliminary image of damage to the thermal protective tiles.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Endeavour successfully docked with the International Space Station at 18:02 UTC (14:02 EDT). Approximately an hour before docking, Endeavour performed the one-degree-per-second backflip, called the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rendezvous_Pitch_Maneuver" title="Rendezvous Pitch Maneuver">\n        Rendezvous Pitch Maneuver\n       </a>\n       (RPM), so the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS" title="ISS">\n        ISS\n       </a>\n       crew members could take digital pictures of the heat shield of the orbiter. The images were then analyzed by NASA\'s Image Analysis Team, as well as the Mission Management Team to inspect the integrity of the orbiter\'s heat shield. Following a series of leak checks, the hatches were opened at 20:04 UTC (16:04 EDT), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Expedition_15" title="Expedition 15">\n        Expedition 15\n       </a>\n       crew welcomed the STS-118 crew aboard the station.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After preliminary review of the photos taken by the Expedition 15 crew during the RPM, an area of interest was discovered on the underside of the Shuttle; an area behind the right landing gear door covered with black\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silica" title="Silica">\n        silica\n       </a>\n       tiles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orbiter_Systems_-_Thermal_Protection_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Orbiter_Systems_-_Thermal_Protection-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The tile directly aft of the door had a 3.5 inches (8.9\xc2\xa0cm) by 2 inches (5.1\xc2\xa0cm) gouge in it. While the tile was penetrated, the underlying felt backing was not. NASA noted in the press conference that launch-time video confirmed a foam strike. This area is less critical than the leading-edge\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reinforced_carbon-carbon" title="Reinforced carbon-carbon">\n        reinforced carbon-carbon\n       </a>\n       tiles that were damaged in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        Space Shuttle Columbia disaster\n       </a>\n       , but did cause concern for the Mission Management Team. A focused inspection was scheduled for 12 August 2007 to determine whether a patch attempt would be undertaken by the astronauts during an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">\n        EVA\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SR-24_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SR-24-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA once reported that pieces of foam are bound to, and have fallen off of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/External_tank" title="External tank">\n        external tank\n       </a>\n       during the eight and a-half minute ride to\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">\n        orbit\n       </a>\n       . Extraordinarily, an unprecedented three-hundred pieces of foam once struck the underside of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter" title="Orbiter">\n        orbiter\n       </a>\n       during launch.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The crew activated the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Station-to-Shuttle_Power_Transfer_System" title="Station-to-Shuttle Power Transfer System">\n        Station-to-Shuttle Power Transfer System\n       </a>\n       (SSPTS) after docking.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The SSPTS transfers electrical power from the station to the shuttle, allowing the shuttle to conserve its own power generating resources. An extension of the mission from 11 to 14 days was dependent on proper operation of the SSPTS.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Saturday_11_August_(Flight_day_4)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Saturday_11_August_.28Flight_day_4.29">\n        Saturday 11 August (Flight day 4)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Saturday 11 August (Flight day 4)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_EVA1_Rick_Mastracchio.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/STS-118_EVA1_Rick_Mastracchio.jpg/220px-STS-118_EVA1_Rick_Mastracchio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/STS-118_EVA1_Rick_Mastracchio.jpg/330px-STS-118_EVA1_Rick_Mastracchio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/STS-118_EVA1_Rick_Mastracchio.jpg/440px-STS-118_EVA1_Rick_Mastracchio.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_EVA1_Rick_Mastracchio.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Astronaut Rick Mastracchio works on the outside of the\n         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n          International Space Station\n         </a>\n         during EVA 1 on 11 August.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       At 21:45 (UTC),\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Mastracchio" title="Richard Mastracchio">\n        Rick Mastracchio\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Williams" title="Dafydd Williams">\n        Dave Williams\n       </a>\n       started the first EVA of the mission, installing the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P5_spacer_truss_segment" title="P5 spacer truss segment">\n        S5 truss\n       </a>\n       to the station, increasing the total mass of the ISS to 232,693 kilograms (513,000\xc2\xa0lb). The EVA duration was 6 hours and 17 minutes, and all objectives were successfully completed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the Mission Status press conference, Lead ISS\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flight_Director" title="Flight Director">\n        Flight Director\n       </a>\n       Joel Montalbano reported that the SSPTS was working well, and the recommendation to the Mission Management Team will be to extend the mission to the planned 14-day mission.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Mission Management Team chair John Shannon reported after additional analysis, it appeared that a piece of foam came off the external tank in the area of the tank\'s feed line, and bounced off a nearby strut, resulting in a hit to the orbiter\'s underside. An almost identical section of foam was lost on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-115" title="STS-115">\n        STS-115\n       </a>\n       , but did not strike the orbiter. John reported after further review of photos taken on flight day three, they do not feel the damage went all the way through the tile, but focused inspection is still planned for flight day five, and decisions would not be made until more information is obtained. Five specific areas will be inspected during focused inspection, and with the data gathered, thermal testing can be done to determine what actions, if any, need to be taken.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Overall, John Shannon classified the foam loss as a "concern", but only with regards to the history that the specific area has with regards to foam loss in past missions. Shannon reported that analysis would be complete by flight day 7 at the latest.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       John Shannon also reported that the possible protruding gap filler noticed on flight day 3, was reviewed further, and was determined to be "shim stock", which will burn off in the upper atmosphere, and poses no issues for re-entry.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Sunday_12_August_(Flight_day_5)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sunday_12_August_.28Flight_day_5.29">\n        Sunday 12 August (Flight day 5)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sunday 12 August (Flight day 5)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Damaged_TPS_Tiles_of_Endeavour_(NASA_S118-E-06229).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1250" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Damaged_TPS_Tiles_of_Endeavour_%28NASA_S118-E-06229%29.jpg/220px-Damaged_TPS_Tiles_of_Endeavour_%28NASA_S118-E-06229%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Damaged_TPS_Tiles_of_Endeavour_%28NASA_S118-E-06229%29.jpg/330px-Damaged_TPS_Tiles_of_Endeavour_%28NASA_S118-E-06229%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Damaged_TPS_Tiles_of_Endeavour_%28NASA_S118-E-06229%29.jpg/440px-Damaged_TPS_Tiles_of_Endeavour_%28NASA_S118-E-06229%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Damaged_TPS_Tiles_of_Endeavour_(NASA_S118-E-06229).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         High resolution image of thermal protective tiles taken during focused inspection on flight day five.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The crew carried out the focused inspection without any problems, and at 20:56 (UTC), the crews of\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       and Expedition 15 were notified that the SSPTS was working as expected, and the mission was officially extended to the planned 14 day mission. Commander Scott Kelly replied, "That\'s great news, thanks".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Status_report_STS-118-09_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Status_report_STS-118-09-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the daily mission status briefing, Lead Flight Director Matt Abbott announced the official extension of the mission, that the SSPTS was working as planned, and they were pleased with the data gathered during the focused inspection on Sunday. Mission Management Team Chairman John Shannon confirmed the decision of the Mission Management Team to extend the mission to 14 days, and to add a fourth EVA, was unanimous. He noted that the addition of SSPTS will be a valuable new tool, providing not only extended missions, but also the ability to provide the space station with additional supplies of oxygen, water, and other resources.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shannon reported on the focused inspection, confirming that good laser data and imagery was obtained, and they resolved several areas of interest, classifying them as of no concern. One area of interest was two adjacent thermal plates on the shuttle\'s underside that had a gouge that appeared to be deeper than would allow them to rule it out. NASA would use data from the focused inspection to model the area, and do thermal analysis of the area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They will use the data to mimic the damage with sample tiles at\n       <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">\n        Johnson Space Center\n       </a>\n       , and using a variety of testing methods, possible courses of action would then be evaluated. No decision would be made until all data had been received and reviewed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shannon did report that following STS-118, NASA will do a thorough review of the history of foam loss from the area of the external tank since\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-114" title="STS-114">\n        STS-114\n       </a>\n       , analysis and testing would be done, and any speculation as to a future course of action would not be made until all the information was available.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Monday_13_August_(Flight_day_6)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Monday_13_August_.28Flight_day_6.29">\n        Monday 13 August (Flight day 6)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Monday 13 August (Flight day 6)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Rick Mastracchio and Dave Williams completed the mission\'s second spacewalk, successfully achieving all of the scheduled activities. During the EVA, they removed a new CMG from\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\'\n       </i>\n       s payload bay, and moved it to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Z1_truss" title="Z1 truss">\n        Z1 truss\n       </a>\n       , where they removed the failed CMG. After installing the new CMG, they placed the failed CMG on an external stowage platform, where it will remain until it is returned to Earth with mission\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-122" title="STS-122">\n        STS-122\n       </a>\n       . After initial testing on the ground, NASA reported the new CMG was functioning normally.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the EVA, Mastracchio reported an EVA suit alarm, indicating high levels of\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         CO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </a>\n       , but after reviewing all indicators and sensors, NASA confirmed it was an instrumentation issue, and the suit itself was fine. At the mission status briefing, NASA reported the suit would be used on future spacewalks, and the issue was not of any concern.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SR_43_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SR_43-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the Mission Management briefing, John Shannon discussed Endeavour\'s heat shield and re-entry issues. He reported that after initial modeling they believe the majority of heating will be on the backside of the gouge, and not into the filler bar side, which was the preferable situation. He reiterated that it was a complicated aerodynamic shape, and they wanted to be sure the flow would concentrate in the back "well" of the hole. The engineers and analysts would continue to do additional flow modeling, after which they would take the data into the arc jet testing facility for additional analysis. The first preliminary arc jet tests would be performed Monday night.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shannon reported a "team four" had been assembled, along with the operations and engineering teams, to assist in data analysis. The teams will look at options for repair if required, and make recommendations to the Mission Management Team after the analysis of tests and data. Shannon stated he had no doubt that if a repair was required, the crew could execute it without significant impact to the mission timeline. He reiterated that this was\n       <i>\n        not\n       </i>\n       a catastrophic damage situation, but simply a situation that they would prefer to fix if possible, similar to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbital_Maneuvering_System" title="Orbital Maneuvering System">\n        OMS\n       </a>\n       blanket issue during STS-117 in June 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SR_44_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SR_44-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are three different on-orbit repair techniques available to the crew. Both post-\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       Return to Flight missions experimented with various repair materials and techniques, and the STS-118 crew has trained for those procedures.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Tuesday_14_August_(Flight_day_7)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tuesday_14_August_.28Flight_day_7.29">\n        Tuesday 14 August (Flight day 7)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tuesday 14 August (Flight day 7)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_ESP-3_on_RMS.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/STS-118_ESP-3_on_RMS.jpg/220px-STS-118_ESP-3_on_RMS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/STS-118_ESP-3_on_RMS.jpg/330px-STS-118_ESP-3_on_RMS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/STS-118_ESP-3_on_RMS.jpg/440px-STS-118_ESP-3_on_RMS.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_ESP-3_on_RMS.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Backdropped by Earth,\n         <i>\n          Endeavour\'\n         </i>\n         s\n         <a href="/wiki/Canadarm" title="Canadarm">\n          Canadarm\n         </a>\n         moves the external stowage platform (ESP-3).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       crew awoke on Tuesday to the voices of Tracy Caldwell\'s family singing happy birthday to her. The two crews successfully removed the ESP-3 from\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\'\n       </i>\n       s payload bay, and installed it onto the\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure#P3.2FP4.2C_S3.2FS4_truss_assemblies" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n        P3\n       </a>\n       truss. They also continued with transfer activities, and several crew members took time out to have two Public Affairs events, one of them answering children\'s questions from the Discovery Center in\n       <a href="/wiki/Boise,_Idaho" title="Boise, Idaho">\n        Boise, Idaho\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During an interview with CBS, Commander Kelly stated that he was not concerned about the tile damage, and would be comfortable with any decision NASA made, "My understanding is this tile damage is not an issue of the safety of the crew... I\'m not concerned with our safety."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The main reason for fixing it, he noted, would be to assist with processing once the orbiter was back at the Kennedy Space Center.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the Mission Management Team briefing, Kirk Shireman, Deputy International Space Station Program Manager, reported that the External Stowage Platform installation went well; the new CMG was working well, and handover of attitude control directly from the shuttle to the station was completed without problems. In addition, a new Russian computer was installed on the station, and testing of the system would be performed in late August. He also mentioned several of the experiments that were launched with STS-118, and reported all experiments were proceeding well. Shireman also noted that as of 15:17 UTC, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Zarya" title="Zarya">\n        Zarya\n       </a>\n       module of the station had orbited the Earth 50,000 times.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       John Shannon reported that the orbiter systems were in excellent shape, and had no issues. With regards to the remaining area of tile damage on the underside of the orbiter, Shannon reported that initial thermal analysis had been completed. Computational fluid dynamics testing at\n       <a href="/wiki/Ames_Research_Center" title="Ames Research Center">\n        Ames Research Center\n       </a>\n       had been done, and the preliminary results were "cautiously optimistic". Testing at the arc jet facility would continue Tuesday night. Shannon stated they would go through complete EVA scenario testing at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutral_Buoyancy_Lab" title="Neutral Buoyancy Lab">\n        Neutral Buoyancy Lab\n       </a>\n       , to help develop the EVA procedures if needed.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Wednesday_15_August_(Flight_day_8)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wednesday_15_August_.28Flight_day_8.29">\n        Wednesday 15 August (Flight day 8)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Wednesday 15 August (Flight day 8)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div
