</div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_glove_damage.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="475" data-file-width="722" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/STS-118_glove_damage.jpg/220px-STS-118_glove_damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/STS-118_glove_damage.jpg/330px-STS-118_glove_damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/STS-118_glove_damage.jpg/440px-STS-118_glove_damage.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_glove_damage.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Mastracchio\'s damaged glove.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Rick Mastracchio and Clayton Anderson began the third EVA of the mission at 14:37 UTC. During the EVA, they successfully relocated a CETA Cart, retrieved the P6 Transponder, relocated the S-band antenna from P6 to P1, and installed a new S-Band Baseband Signal Processor and Transponder on the P1 truss. During a routine glove inspection, Mastracchio noticed a possible tear on the thumb of his left glove.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       To be safe, NASA managers decided to end the spacewalk at 20:05, and examination and photography of the glove was performed during suit removal. The spacewalk accomplished all but one of the tasks (MISSE retrieval).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On the station, the crewmembers continued with transfer activities.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the Mission Management Team briefing, Joel Montalbano reported that the issue with Mastracchio\'s suit was never a danger to the suit integrity, and the decision to cut the EVA short was one of precaution. Extended photography was performed, and additional analysis will be completed prior to the fourth EVA. Montalbano reported that the fourth EVA would be no earlier than 18 August 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Lead spacewalk officer Paul Boehm agreed that the EVA went well, the major objectives were completed, and he reiterated that at no time was Mastracchio\'s suit in any danger of leaking.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       EVA Office Manager Steve Doering reported on the details regarding the issue with Mastracchio\'s glove. The EVA inspection procedure was implemented following STS-116, when a cut was found on\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Curbeam" title="Robert Curbeam">\n        Robert Curbeam\n       </a>\n       \'s glove following an EVA. The EVA suit comprises five layers of material, and the second layer, called\n       <a href="/wiki/Vectran" title="Vectran">\n        vectran\n       </a>\n       , is a high strength material resistant to tearing. Mastracchio\'s tear was into the vectran layer. Prior to the next EVA, video analysis will be done of the path Mastracchio took during the spacewalk in an attempt to discover where the tear may have occurred. An analysis of Mastracchio\'s glove during the previous two EVAs will also be performed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       John Shannon reported that no decision had been made regarding the tile damage on the underside of the orbiter, but the fourth EVA was postponed to at least 18 August 2007. The management team would continue to analyze the potential risks of repair to the underside of the orbiter, as well as any other areas of risk. Shannon reported the results of the arc jet testing showed some erosion into the backside of the adjacent tile upon re-entry, but the erosion did not go through the entire layer of the tile. Preliminary results were encouraging, but additional testing would be performed on Wednesday night. Shannon reported that the final decision would most likely be made on Thursday.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Shannon said "I am cautiously optimistic that repairs will not be needed".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:186643main_iss015e22561_hires.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/186643main_iss015e22561_hires.jpg/220px-186643main_iss015e22561_hires.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/186643main_iss015e22561_hires.jpg/330px-186643main_iss015e22561_hires.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/186643main_iss015e22561_hires.jpg/440px-186643main_iss015e22561_hires.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:186643main_iss015e22561_hires.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Astronaut\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clay_Anderson" title="Clay Anderson">\n          Clay Anderson\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Expedition_15" title="Expedition 15">\n          Expedition 15\n         </a>\n         flight engineer, uses a digital camera to expose a photo of his helmet visor during the mission\'s third EVA.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Thursday_16_August_(Flight_day_9)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Thursday_16_August_.28Flight_day_9.29">\n        Thursday 16 August (Flight day 9)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Thursday 16 August (Flight day 9)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The station and shuttle crews continued transfer activities on flight day 9, as well as EVA preparations, which included\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_thermal_protection_system" title="Space Shuttle thermal protection system">\n        TPS\n       </a>\n       repair procedure review, in case NASA decided a repair was necessary.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Mission Specialists Barbara Morgan and Alvin Drew participated in an education event in the morning with students at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Challenger_Center_for_Space_Science_Education" title="Challenger Center for Space Science Education">\n        Challenger Center for Space Science Education\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexandria,_Virginia" title="Alexandria, Virginia">\n        Alexandria\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       . The event was hosted by Dr. June Scobee Rogers, wife of\n       <i>\n        Challenger\'\n       </i>\n       s commander,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dick_Scobee" title="Dick Scobee">\n        Dick Scobee\n       </a>\n       , and Founding Chairman of the Challenger Center. Morgan and Drew also spoke to reporters from the Associated Press, Reuters and Idaho Public Television.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the interview with Reuters, Drew stated "We\'ve been talking to the engineers who have been analyzing this far more than we have in space, and they seem to feel that the biggest danger is more to just being able to re-use\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       once it gets back on the ground. They seem to be confident, and I trust their confidence that we can get home safely even with the divot that we have in the belly,"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Morgan added "We have a lot of faith in the program, and we\'ll do what the engineers decide is the best thing for us to do. We have all confidence we\'re going to be able to do the right thing."\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At 01:00 UTC, 17 August 2007, CAPCOM\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shane_Kimbrough" title="Shane Kimbrough">\n        Shane Kimbrough\n       </a>\n       notified commander Kelly that the Mission Management Team decided that no repair to the damaged tile on the underside of the orbiter would be required.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the Mission Management Team briefing, John Shannon announced the team\'s unanimous decision that an EVA to repair the damaged tile was not required, and the tile damage on the underside of the orbiter was not a threat to crew safety. However, the spacewalk to repair the damage could pose a variety of risks, and those risks weighed heavily into the final decision. He noted the arc jet tests actually showed a higher degree of damage than the orbiter would sustain during re-entry, so the tests were helpful in showing the worst "possible" damage, and still did not damage the tile during testing enough to warrant repair.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shannon did note that the JSC Engineering Independent Group advised NASA managers that repairing the damage on-orbit could assist with mission turn-around time once the orbiter was on the ground. Shannon noted that the risks associated with in-flight repair outweighed the possible delay in processing the orbiter following the mission. He stated that normal turn-around time would not be compromised, as most orbiters have at least 60 tiles replaced after each mission, so the situation would not be any different than past missions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When pressed during the briefing by a reporter as to the chance of shuttle or crew loss, Shannon reported "I am 100 percent comfortable that the work that has been done, has accurately characterized the damage, and that we will have a very successful re-entry". He stated that over 200 people were involved in the decision, representing over 30 organizations, including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_Ames_Research_Center" title="NASA Ames Research Center">\n        NASA Ames Research Center\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Langley_Research_Center" title="Langley Research Center">\n        NASA\'s Langley Research Center\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">\n        Jet Propulsion Laboratory\n       </a>\n       , KSC,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">\n        JSC\n       </a>\n       , and that all the groups combined came to the same decision.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shannon reported that the glove issue encountered during EVA three had been discussed, and stated that analysis would be continued, in advance of EVA four on Saturday. The crew does have a spare set of gloves, if needed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shannon reported on a micro-meteoroid debris strike discovered on the commander\'s window of the orbiter, which was 1 millimeter in depth. Shannon noted that it was consistent with previous damage sustained on past missions. Analysis would be conducted regarding this issue, using photographs sent down by the crew early Thursday morning.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The final item discussed was\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean_(2007)" title="Hurricane Dean (2007)">\n        Hurricane Dean\n       </a>\n       , which was heading towards the Caribbean Sea, and projected to move into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       . Contingency procedures and plans were in place, but Shannon did not anticipate it would affect the mission\'s timeline at all.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Friday_17_August_(Flight_day_10)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Friday_17_August_.28Flight_day_10.29">\n        Friday 17 August (Flight day 10)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Friday 17 August (Flight day 10)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The station and shuttle crews had a relatively quiet day on flight day 10, continuing transfer operations, and doing some troubleshooting on a communication system between the shuttle and station. The two crews took some time out to have a joint news conference with US and Canadian news agencies, and took the official combined crew portrait.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       When asked by reporters on the ground whether the crew agreed with NASA\'s decision to return without repairing the damage to\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\'\n       </i>\n       s underside, Commander Kelly replied, "We agree absolutely 100 percent with the decision to not repair the damage."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the mission status briefing, Lead Flight Director Matt Abbott discussed the ongoing preparations and plans with regards to Hurricane Dean, and reported NASA was watching the storm\'s track closely. If required, contingency plans are available. While the mission\'s timeline could be changed if required, no decision was made, and the mission was proceeding as planned.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Deputy ISS Program Manager Kirk Shireman reported the S-Band system relocated during the third EVA was working well, and the SSPTS provided enough oxygen to be able to completely fill all reserves on the station. Shireman commented that transfer operations were approximately 75% complete.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       EVA Office Manager Steve Doering reported on the decision to proceed with Saturday\'s EVA. The team analyzed the video downlinked from the third EVA, and the review showed no evidence of any specific event that would indicate a sharp edge, or excessive wear. A review of the manufacturing of the gloves was done, and no concerns were identified. The paths taken by astronauts during spacewalks were reviewed, identifying common paths between the third EVA, and Saturday\'s planned EVA, and the crew was notified of the common locations, to identify areas where additional glove inspections would be performed on Saturday. Overall, the final EVA would be less "hand-intensive" than the previous spacewalks, and the conclusion following the analysis was that Saturday\'s EVA would go ahead as planned.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Saturday_18_August_(Flight_day_11)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Saturday_18_August_.28Flight_day_11.29">\n        Saturday 18 August (Flight day 11)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Saturday 18 August (Flight day 11)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MISSE_STS-118.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MISSE_STS-118.jpg/220px-MISSE_STS-118.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MISSE_STS-118.jpg/330px-MISSE_STS-118.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MISSE_STS-118.jpg/440px-MISSE_STS-118.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MISSE_STS-118.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         One of the retrieved MISSE experiments.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       NASA Managers decided overnight to shorten the fourth EVA by two hours as a precaution due to\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean" title="Hurricane Dean">\n        Hurricane Dean\n       </a>\n       \'s continued path into the Gulf of Mexico.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The EVA duration was five hours and 2 minutes, with a total EVA time of 23 hours and 15 minutes for the mission. The EVA accomplished three primary objectives, and one get-ahead task. Two tasks were deferred: plans to tie down debris shields on the Destiny lab, and relocation of a tool box.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the spacewalk, Williams and Anderson got a good look at Hurricane Dean, and were both awed at the sight. "Holy smoke" was Anderon\'s initial comment. "Man, that\'s impressive", Williams replied. Anderson added "They\'re only impressive when they\'re not coming towards you."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SR-65_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SR-65-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Transfer activities were completed ahead of schedule, and both crews worked hard to get everything transferred back to\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       after the spacewalk.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Dave Williams set two records during his third EVA; He is the Canadian with the most spacewalks (3); and he passed Canadian Astronaut\n       <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hadfield" title="Chris Hadfield">\n        Chris Hadfield\n       </a>\n       in total EVA time. Williams ended Saturday\'s EVA with a total of 17 hours, 47 minutes of extravehicular time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HurricaneDean.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2004" data-file-width="3032" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/HurricaneDean.jpg/220px-HurricaneDean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/HurricaneDean.jpg/330px-HurricaneDean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/HurricaneDean.jpg/440px-HurricaneDean.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HurricaneDean.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         View of Hurricane Dean taken from the International Space Station during the fourth STS-118 EVA.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       During the mission status briefing, Launch Integration Manager\n       <a href="/wiki/LeRoy_E._Cain" title="LeRoy E. Cain">\n        LeRoy Cain\n       </a>\n       reported that the Mission Management Team decided to take extra precautions in preparation for the storm, and STS-118 would be cut short a day.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the event of a hurricane evacuation in Houston, an emergency command center would need to be set up. While it was a contingency set in place for years, NASA would prefer to avoid that situation. To that end, Cain reported the EVA was shortened, and the hatch closure would be done Saturday evening, rather than Sunday as planned. Undocking would be at 11:57 UTC Sunday, with the first KSC Landing opportunity on 21 August 2007.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At 19:46, a short farewell ceremony was performed, followed by hatch closure at 20:10 UTC. Tuesday\'s tentative KSC landing time would be 12:32\xc2\xa0pm EST. (16:30 UTC)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Sunday_19_August_(Flight_day_12)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sunday_19_August_.28Flight_day_12.29">\n        Sunday 19 August (Flight day 12)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sunday 19 August (Flight day 12)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS-118_in_August_2007.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1872" data-file-width="2928" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/ISS_after_STS-118_in_August_2007.jpg/220px-ISS_after_STS-118_in_August_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/ISS_after_STS-118_in_August_2007.jpg/330px-ISS_after_STS-118_in_August_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/ISS_after_STS-118_in_August_2007.jpg/440px-ISS_after_STS-118_in_August_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS-118_in_August_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The International Space Station moves away from Space Shuttle Endeavour during STS-118\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       successfully undocked from the International Space Station at 11:56 UTC. Saturday, NASA managers decided the station fly-around that is normally performed following each mission would not be conducted in order to give the Shuttle crew more free time during flight day 12. After several long work days, the Mission Control team felt the crew needed some downtime before the landing process began.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After undocking, two 4-second firings of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reaction_Control_System" title="Reaction Control System">\n        Reaction Control System\n       </a>\n       were performed, in order to distance\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       from the station and move to a position above it. There, the crew deployed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Boom_Sensor_System" title="Orbiter Boom Sensor System">\n        robotic arm\n       </a>\n       , beginning Late Inspection of the reinforced carbon-carbon tiles on the nose cap and wing leading edges.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At the mission status briefing, Matt Abbott reported the undocking was "flawless", and the late inspection was completed successfully. Monday would be a standard pre-landing day, with checkout of the various systems on\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       , as well as an educational media event. Entry Flight Director Steve Stich and the entry team will take over mission duties tonight, in preparation for Tuesday\'s landing.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       John Shannon reported the mission management team meeting went well. The landing plan was reviewed, and all teams reported "go" for landing on Tuesday. The latest track for Hurricane Dean was favorable for the Houston area; the storm seemed to be swinging farther south than originally expected. NASA managers were optimistic that contingency plans would not be needed. Final decisions regarding alternate plans would not be made until Monday, but Shannon noted that\n       <a href="/wiki/White_Sands_Missile_Range#NASA_use" title="White Sands Missile Range">\n        White Sands Space Harbor\n       </a>\n       landing facility would be removed as an alternate site.\n       <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">\n        Edwards Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       , and Kennedy Shuttle Landing Facility would be the two sites evaluated on Monday.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Monday_20_August_(Flight_day_13)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Monday_20_August_.28Flight_day_13.29">\n        Monday 20 August (Flight day 13)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Monday 20 August (Flight day 13)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       On Monday, with the shuttle approximately 68 miles (109\xc2\xa0km) behind the International Space Station, the crew of\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       performed a variety of check-out tests in preparation for entry, configured the Spacehab module for entry, and did some last minute stowage. Kelly and Hobaugh worked with the shuttle landing simulator on board, practicing the anticipated landing tracks. Kelly, Williams and Morgan took some time out to talk to students at the Canadian school, La Ronge, in Saskatchewan.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the mission status briefing, Entry Flight Director Steve Stich reported the track of Hurricane Dean would not require the activation of contingency plans, and the forecast looked favorable for a Tuesday landing at Kennedy Shuttle Landing Facility.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There were also two opportunities for a Florida landing, with the first opportunity beginning with a deorbit burn at 15:25 UTC, and landing at 16:32 UTC. The second opportunity would call for a deorbit burn at 17:00 UTC, with landing at 18:16 UTC. Weather was not expected to interfere with landing, with a forecast of high clouds, but no inclement weather. If the second landing opportunity was taken, the shuttle would fly directly over Hurricane Dean, although it would be well above any effects of the storm. NASA did plan to call up Edwards Air Force Base as the backup site, which had two opportunities on Tuesday, but the plan was to attempt a KSC landing, and if both opportunities were waved off, NASA would decide whether to wait a day, and try for a Wednesday landing at KSC. If Wednesday opportunities at Florida were waved off due to weather, a landing at Edwards Air Force Base would be attempted.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Tuesday_21_August_(Flight_day_14,_Landing)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tuesday_21_August_.28Flight_day_14.2C_Landing.29">\n        Tuesday 21 August (Flight day 14, Landing)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tuesday 21 August (Flight day 14, Landing)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_shuttle_Endeavour_STS-118_landing.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Space_shuttle_Endeavour_STS-118_landing.jpg/220px-Space_shuttle_Endeavour_STS-118_landing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Space_shuttle_Endeavour_STS-118_landing.jpg/330px-Space_shuttle_Endeavour_STS-118_landing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Space_shuttle_Endeavour_STS-118_landing.jpg/440px-Space_shuttle_Endeavour_STS-118_landing.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_shuttle_Endeavour_STS-118_landing.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Endeavour\n         </i>\n         landing at Kennedy Space Center.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The crew of\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       went right to work after waking up on Tuesday, completing the close-out of the Spacehab module, and getting into the deorbit preparations timeline.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They closed payload bay doors, transitioned the vehicle computers to landing software mode and donned their reentry suits. At 14:30 UTC, the crew was given the "go" to begin fluid loading. This was done to assist with the crew\'s ability to adjust to gravity, and to prevent\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypotension" title="Hypotension">\n        hypotension\n       </a>\n       after landing. At 12:30 UTC, the Space Flight\n       <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">\n        Meteorology\n       </a>\n       Group reported to Entry Team Flight Director Steve Stich that the weather forecast was a "go". The weather at Kennedy Space Center showed only scattered showers moving away from the landing facility, and cross winds were not expected to be a problem. At 15:08 UTC, the crew was given a "go" for the deorbit burn, and the auxiliary power units were started at 15:20 UTC. The 4 minute engine burn was successfully completed at 15:28 UTC, slowing\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       by approximately 252 miles per hour, (405 kilometres (252\xc2\xa0mi)/h) and adjusting the orbiter\'s trajectory correctly for landing.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Radar acquisition of\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       through\n       <a href="/wiki/Merritt_Island_Spaceflight_Tracking_and_Data_Network_station" title="Merritt Island Spaceflight Tracking and Data Network station">\n        MILA\n       </a>\n       happened at 16:19 UTC. At 16:20 UTC, the shuttle had passed the area of peak heating, with no issues reported on board. Main landing gear touchdown occurred at 16:32:16 UTC with nose gear touchdown at 16:32:29 UTC. The orbiter came to a complete stop at 16:33:20 UTC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Upon wheel stop,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CAPCOM" title="CAPCOM">\n        CAPCOM\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Ferguson" title="Christopher Ferguson">\n        Christopher Ferguson\n       </a>\n       told the crew, "Congratulations, you\'ve given a new meaning to the term \'higher education.\'"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_damaged_tile.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/STS-118_damaged_tile.jpg/220px-STS-118_damaged_tile.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/STS-118_damaged_tile.jpg/330px-STS-118_damaged_tile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/STS-118_damaged_tile.jpg/440px-STS-118_damaged_tile.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_damaged_tile.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Damaged tile in the belly of\n         <i>\n          Endeavour\n         </i>\n         during post-landing inspection.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Initial post-landing inspection of the orbiter showed very little additional damage to the thermal tiles affected by the foam strike during launch. Barbara Morgan did not exit the crew transport vehicle with the rest of the crew; she remained on board the vehicle to receive additional medical tests, and would return to the Astronaut Crew Quarters in that vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The remaining six crew members briefly examined the orbiter, doing the traditional post-flight "walkaround", posed for photos, and then returned to the crew quarters in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronaut_transfer_van" title="Astronaut transfer van">\n        Astrovan\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the post-landing briefing, NASA Administrator Michael D. Griffin reported that the International Space Station was approximately 60% completed following STS-118. Griffin also stressed the importance of space exploration, and added that the damaged tile on the underside of the orbiter did very well during re-entry.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Associate Administrator for Spaceflight Operations\n       <a href="/wiki/William_H._Gerstenmaier" title="William H. Gerstenmaier">\n        William H. Gerstenmaier\n       </a>\n       reported the damage was actually less than what the arc jet testing produced, a situation that NASA anticipated, and managers had earlier stressed that arc jets show "worst possible" damage. Launch and Entry Flight Director Mike Leinbach stressed how pleased he was with the mission, and with the condition of the vehicle following re-entry. He stated it was "one of the cleanest vehicles the managers have seen since the Return to Flight policies were implemented, if not the cleanest."\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At the end of the briefing, Griffin commented to the media who focused on Barbara Morgan being the first "teacher in space", that Morgan was not technically a "teacher in space", nor was she an "Educator Astronaut". He stated she was accepted as a Mission Specialist, before the new class of Mission Specialist Educators were selected in 2004, and NASA considers her to be a mission specialist, who was once a teacher.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michael118_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-michael118-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, NASA does refer to Morgan as a Mission Specialist Educator in a number of interviews, so the terms seem to be interchangeable to most, if not to Griffin.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the post-landing crew press conference, Kelly was asked "Did the tile damage enter your mind at all during re-entry, and what did you think about it once you got a look during the walkaround?" Kelly\'s reply was, "I thought about it, but only because I knew I\'d be asked about it. I didn\'t worry about it at all. I was underwhelmed by it."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n       <tr>\n        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 60px; font-family: \'Times New Roman\', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\n         \xe2\x80\x9c\n        </td>\n        <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">\n         <i>\n          You know, there\'s a great sense of pride to be able to be involved in a human endeavor that takes us all a little bit farther, when you look down and see our Earth... and you realize what we are trying to do as a human race, it\'s pretty profound.\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 60px; font-family: \'Times New Roman\', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\n         \xe2\x80\x9d\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td class="cquotecite" colspan="3" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller;       </a>\n          </sup>\n         </cite>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Extra-vehicular_activity">\n        Extra-vehicular   <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wake-up_calls">\n        Wake-up calls\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Wake-up calls">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       NASA began a tradition of playing music to astronauts during the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gemini_program" title="Gemini program">\n        Gemini program\n       </a>\n       , which was first used to wake up a flight crew during\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">\n        Apollo 15\n       </a>\n       . Each track is specially chosen, often by their family, and usually has special meaning to an individual member of the crew, or is applicable to their daily activities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Day 2: "\n        <a href="http://spaceflight.nasa.gov/gallery/audio/shuttle/sts-118/mp3/fd14.mp3" rel="nofollow">\n         mp3\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contingency_mission">\n        Contingency mission\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-118&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Contingency mission">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-3xx" title="STS-3xx">\n        STS-322\n       </a>\n       was the designation given to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contingency_Shuttle_Crew_Support" title="Contingency Shuttle Crew Support">\n        Contingency Shuttle Crew Support\n       </a>\n       mission which would have been launched in the event\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n        Space Shuttle Endeavour\n       </a>\n       had become disabled during STS-118.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It would have been a modified version of the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-120" title="STS-120">\n        STS-120\n       </a>\n       mission, which would have involved the launch date being brought forward. If it had been needed, it would have been launched no earlier than 22 September 2007. The crew for this mission would have been a four-person subset of the full STS-120 crew.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">\n        Media\n       </span>\n
